"author_association": "NONE", "pull_request": {"url": "https://api.github.com/repos/y785/moe-scheduler/pulls/3", "html_url": "https://github.com/y785/moe-scheduler/pull/3", "diff_url": "https://github.com/y785/moe-scheduler/pull/3.diff", "patch_url": "https://github.com/y785/moe-scheduler/pull/3.patch"}, "body": "Typically, when you want to create a timed-task and cancel it, you had to physically find the task, a scheduler that has been used, and invoke either `unregister(MoeTask task)` or `remove(Predicate<MoeTask> check)` from `MoeScheduler.java`. While this is a perfectly valid way to cancel the task, it is often tedious and prone to errors, particularly when you are using multiple schedulers. To combat this, I have created a new interface `MoeFutureTask` that inherits from `MoeTask` that allows for timed-tasks to be cancelled by simply invoking `cancel()` method. This way, one do not need to search for scheduler that has been registered on. Additionally, invoking `registerDelayed` method from `MoeScheduler.java` now returns `MoeFutureTask` that can be used to be stored as a variable and cancelled whenever desired.\r\n\r\nExample usage:\r\nBefore\r\n```java\r\nvar task = new MoeDelayedTask((delta) -> doSomething(), 10000);\r\nscheduler.register(task);\r\n//After some time....\r\nscheduler.unregister(task);\r\n```\r\nAfter\r\n```java\r\nvar task = scheduler.registerDelayed((delta) -> doSomething(), 10000);\r\n//After some time...\r\ntask.cancel() //Returns true if successful\r\n```\r\n"}, "comment": {"url": "https://api.github.com/repos/y785/moe-scheduler/issues/comments/567356113", "html_url": "https://github.com/y785/moe-scheduler/pull/3#issuecomment-567356113", "issue_url": "https://api.github.com/repos/y785/moe-scheduler/issues/3", "id": 567356113, "node_id": "MDEyOklzc3VlQ29tbWVudDU2NzM1NjExMw==", "user": {"login": "y785", "id": 40402540, "node_id": "MDQ6VXNlcjQwNDAyNTQw", "avatar_url": "https://avatars1.githubusercontent.com/u/40402540?v=4", "gravatar_id": "", "url": "https://api.github.com/users/y785", "html_url": "https://github.com/y785", "followers_url": "https://api.github.com/users/y785/followers", "following_url": "https://api.github.com/users/y785/following{/other_user}", "gists_url": "https://api.github.com/users/y785/gists{/gist_id}", "starred_url": "https://api.github.com/users/y785/starred{/owner}{/repo}", "subscriptions_url": "https://api.github.com/users/y785/subscriptions", "organizations_url": "https://api.github.com/users/y785/orgs", "repos_url": "https://api.github.com/users/y785/repos", "events_url": "https://api.github.com/users/y785/events{/privacy}", "received_events_url": "https://api.github.com/users/y785/received_events", "type": "User", "site_admin": false}, "created_at": "2019-12-19T06:35:51Z", "updated_at": "2019-12-19T06:35:51Z", "author_association": "OWNER", "body": "If the task needs to be cancelled, would a ``void cancel() { this.done = true; }`` not suffice? While I don't use locks for this project(or in the example implementation) there have been use cases in my personal projects.\r\n\r\nLet me know if the provided solution would help."}}, "public":
